  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_34d6b08e-2742-4f2c-bb10-935f09971ef1'
      });

  <span id="freeText4035704781476490117" style="display:none">When a dragon storms the castle, what should a (virgin) princess do?<br /><br />Why, turn to her studies, of course! But nothing practical-minded Princess Andromeda of Acadia finds gives a definitive solution. The only Traditional answer, though, is soothing the marauding dragon by a virgin sacrifice. Things are going fairly smoothly with the lottery--except for the women chosen, of course--until Princess Andromeda herself is picked!<br /><br />But facing down the dragon doesn't go quite as planned, and now, with the help of her Champion, Sir George, Andromeda searches for the dragon's lair. But even--<i>especially</i>--in the Five Hundred Kingdoms, bucking Tradition isn't easy. It takes the strongest of wills, knowledge, quick wits and a refusal to give up, no matter what happens along the way....</span>

<div id="review_723339" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/723339" />
    <a title="Debbie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58940-debbie"><img alt="Debbie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604040647p2/58940.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/723339?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debbie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debbie" href="/user/show/58940-debbie">Debbie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780373802173" href="/book/show/638494.One_Good_Knight">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58940-debbie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58940-debbie?shelf=dead-tree">dead-tree</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58940-debbie?shelf=2006">2006</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58940-debbie?shelf=library">library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer723339" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2293327500071446120">I keep reading Lackey's new books because of some misguided sense of author loyalty. I realized a while back that I'd fallen out of love with her writing. Her characters are too one-dimensional, her plotting is cliched and at times forced, the endings are rushed, and her main characters all appear to be variations on the same theme. However, I had enjoyed The Fairy Godmother because it was fresh and original. I was therefore looking forward to this one. It was a let down. All of Lackey's faults </span>
  <span id="freeText2293327500071446120" style="display:none">I keep reading Lackey's new books because of some misguided sense of author loyalty. I realized a while back that I'd fallen out of love with her writing. Her characters are too one-dimensional, her plotting is cliched and at times forced, the endings are rushed, and her main characters all appear to be variations on the same theme. However, I had enjoyed The Fairy Godmother because it was fresh and original. I was therefore looking forward to this one. It was a let down. All of Lackey's faults were highlighted in this book. Plus, the obligatory romance story (it is a Luna book, after all) was thrown in as an afterthought and never fully developed. I'm not sure if this author is worth the aggravation any more. I still love some her older books and often read them for comfort, but I doubt I'll be buying anymore of her stuff. If I have to, I'll borrow from a library.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2293327500071446120" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Lackey fans, fantasy fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/138248-dawn?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2093514" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1573560548585696284"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13978.One_Good_Knight__Five_Hundred_Kingdoms___2_' title='One Good Knight (Five Hundred Kingdoms, #2) by Mercedes Lackey' rel='nofollow noopener'> One Good Knight</a> takes place in the Five Hundred Kingdoms world established by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13631868.The_Fairy_Godmother' title='The Fairy Godmother by Lynsay Sands' rel='nofollow noopener'> The Fairy Godmother</a>. Lackey writes an engaging retelling of the Andromeda sacrifice. Andie, our main character, is a pretty standard Lackey heroine: Spunky, smart, overlooked in intelligence & beauty and yet loved by her commoner friends. Oh yah, and has a mother who secretly hates her and has a dark secret.<br/><br/>At the same time, I don't mind the cliches as much as I would otherwise as Lackey has established that she's pl</span>
  <span id="freeText1573560548585696284" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13978.One_Good_Knight__Five_Hundred_Kingdoms___2_" title="One Good Knight (Five Hundred Kingdoms, #2) by Mercedes Lackey" rel="nofollow noopener"> One Good Knight</a> takes place in the Five Hundred Kingdoms world established by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13631868.The_Fairy_Godmother" title="The Fairy Godmother by Lynsay Sands" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Fairy Godmother</a>. Lackey writes an engaging retelling of the Andromeda sacrifice. Andie, our main character, is a pretty standard Lackey heroine: Spunky, smart, overlooked in intelligence &amp; beauty and yet loved by her commoner friends. Oh yah, and has a mother who secretly hates her and has a dark secret.<br /><br />At the same time, I don't mind the cliches as much as I would otherwise as Lackey has established that she's playing a sandbox where cliche &amp; Tradition is a living force, so all of that makes sense. I liked the mystery set up and I liked some of the side digressions. I was interested in how Lackey handled the Champion coming to Andie's aid without becoming her One True Love. However, it meant that Andie's romance wasn't introduced until page 260 or so of a 450 page book. And the romance wasn't even apparent until more like page 320. I don't have a problem with that per se, except that this was a LUNA book and supposed to have romance as a backbone. As it was, it felt like something more likely to be published as fantasy with the romance tacked on. Additionally, we didn't get a huge amount of lead up for this to have really worked for me in detail. Almost none of the POV from the lover, and yet we had Andie's POV and that of the villians.<br /><br />I'd still recommend this book to anyone who enjoyed Lackey's Fairy Godmother (and Elena does make an appearance here) or to people who enjoy reworking and retelling of fairy tales. But it isn't Lackey's strongest offering and the romance is lacking for anyone seeking that.<br /><br />Though the digression on having democracy in a small midevil kingdom was hilarious.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1573560548585696284" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5142773581360853414">3.5 stars<br/>This was not my favorite book of the <b>Five Hundred Kingdoms</b>, but it wasn't my least favorite, either. <br/><br/>The blurb made me think that <b>One Good Knight</b> started out with a dragon chomping on virgins, but in actuality it takes a while to get to that part of the story.   <span id="freeText5142773581360853414" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br />This was not my favorite book of the <b>Five Hundred Kingdoms</b>, but it wasn't my least favorite, either. <br /><br />The blurb made me think that <b>One Good Knight</b> started out with a dragon chomping on virgins, but in actuality it takes a while to get to that part of the story. There is more going on in this kingdom than meets the eye, as Andie discovers. The twist as the end of the book was cute, unfortunately I already knew about it. I can't remember where I saw the spoiler, but I'm sure it was my own fault for finding out. I've <i>really</i> got to stop doing that. I think if I hadn't known what was going to happen in advance, I might have found it more entertaining. <br />As with most of Lackey's books, the romance is not very in-depth. Yes, characters fall in love, but it isn't the driving force of the plot. So what you're left with is a lighthearted fairytale/fantasy that moves at a decent pace, and has fairly likable characters.<br /><br />Recommended for fans of Lackey and fantasy-lite.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14452194978152122653">After reading and loving Lackey's "The Fairy Godmother", I was a little hesitant to continue the series since so many reviewers seemed to have some major problems with the second installment. I was pleasantly surprised to find that this book held my attention almost as much as its predecessor.<br/><br/>While I must agree that plot elements can be a little predictable and that sometimes the main character's inner dialogue has a tendency to repeat itself, overall I found the kingdom of Acadia and its inhabi</span>
  <span id="freeText14452194978152122653" style="display:none">After reading and loving Lackey's "The Fairy Godmother", I was a little hesitant to continue the series since so many reviewers seemed to have some major problems with the second installment. I was pleasantly surprised to find that this book held my attention almost as much as its predecessor.<br /><br />While I must agree that plot elements can be a little predictable and that sometimes the main character's inner dialogue has a tendency to repeat itself, overall I found the kingdom of Acadia and its inhabitants engaging enough to hold my interest for hours at a time. Princess Andromeda is, in my mind, a well-balanced combination of intelligence, strength, and feminine sweetness. I find it refreshing to spend some time with a heroine who is strong and shows independence without adopting other unintended characterizations like cruelty. I also thoroughly enjoyed the cameos featuring Godmother Elena from the first book, which effectively bridge these two separate kingdoms and remind readers why they fell in love with The Five Hundred Kingdoms in the first place.<br /><br />Those expecting a fairy tale romance might be disappointed to learn that one does not surface until very near the end, but those like myself who are satisfied with exploring this world in which The Tradition (the force behind all fairy tales) lives will be quite content indeed.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10443949474125375751">The first half of this book was pretty good, but boy did it go downhill very abruptly. <br/>Suddenly, the story is riddled with plot holes, instalove, and the same things getting really over explained.<br/><br/>The thing that bothered me the most was this: the main character meets a guy who is all “don’t fall in love with me!” But she blatantly admits (in internal dialogue) that she’s falling in love with him.   <span id="freeText10443949474125375751" style="display:none">The first half of this book was pretty good, but boy did it go downhill very abruptly. <br />Suddenly, the story is riddled with plot holes, instalove, and the same things getting really over explained.<br /><br />The thing that bothered me the most was this: the main character meets a guy who is all “don’t fall in love with me!” But she blatantly admits (in internal dialogue) that she’s falling in love with him. He turns out to be a girl in disguise, and the fact that the main character was attracted to her when she thought she was a boy is never talked about again. <br />As soon as the guy is discovered to be a girl in disguise, I thought there would be an awesome f/f romance. But no. The girls both fall in love with dragons instead, when they pretty much had no chemistry, and it all felt very forced. <br /><br />Overall, this book got off to a great start but the 2nd half made no damned sense at all.<br /><br />Since I normally really like her books, I was pretty disappointed.</span>

<div id="review_3298232091" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3298232091" />
    <a title="Aphelia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/82832336-aphelia"><img alt="Aphelia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528413347p2/82832336.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3298232091?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aphelia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aphelia" href="/user/show/82832336-aphelia">Aphelia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/82832336-aphelia?shelf=my-collection">my-collection</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/82832336-aphelia?shelf=fairy-tale">fairy-tale</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/82832336-aphelia?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/82832336-aphelia?shelf=20for2020tbrchallenge">20for2020tbrchallenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3298232091" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14629407102686454426"><b>#22 of my #20for2020tbrchallenge, to read 20 TBR books in the year 2020</b><br/><br/><b>I've seen some reviews that say this can be read as a standalone, but I highly recommend reading at least the first book (after which you can skip around) for foundational knowledge of the Godmothers and The Tradition, which is magical force combined from folklore, fairy tales and legend that acts upon people by pushing them to fill stereotypical roles and reenact stories for good or evil. Godmothers can magically manipulate </b></span>
  <span id="freeText14629407102686454426" style="display:none"><b>#22 of my #20for2020tbrchallenge, to read 20 TBR books in the year 2020</b><br /><br /><b>I've seen some reviews that say this can be read as a standalone, but I highly recommend reading at least the first book (after which you can skip around) for foundational knowledge of the Godmothers and The Tradition, which is magical force combined from folklore, fairy tales and legend that acts upon people by pushing them to fill stereotypical roles and reenact stories for good or evil. Godmothers can magically manipulate the Tradition and keep it from totally taking over everyday life.</b><br /><br />Although this is only the third book I've read in this series, it is rapidly becoming my favourite Lackey work! <b>BOOKWYRMS. Actual book-hoarding, library-building dragons!!! Need I say more?</b> ❤📚🐲<br /><br />Light, charming and captivating, this is the comfort read I needed right now! It's the story of a Princess' struggle to rid her kingdom, Acadia, of corruption - but evil is very hard to face when it comes in the form of your own mother.<br /><br />Princess Andromeda - Andie - is bookish and practical, much to the obvious disappointment of her beautiful and ruthlessly ambitious mother, Queen Cassiopeia. The Queen wanted a pretty, pliant, passive 'marriage pawn' for a daughter, someone of no threat or consequence beyond being a bargaining chip for political gain.<br /><br />But despite the best efforts of the Queen and her magician councilor Solon to keep her ignorant, Andie has a curious and inquiring mind. She wants to make herself useful to her mother, sure that if she proves that her intelligence can be usefully applied to benefit the interests of the realm then her mother might finally *see* the person she is instead of all the things she is not. <br /><br />So Andie educates herself about the economy, and when she notices serious discrepancies in the Royal Treasury - there have been a highly unlikely number of profitable shipwrecks lately, and some questionable weather is the cause - she brings it to her mother's attention, which is a serious mistake.<br /><br />When a dragon turns up and attacks livestock in the countryside, scaring the populace, it is Andie's researches that uncover the traditional virgin sacrifice solution, which the Queen quickly implements much to Andie's dismay. After a hopeless few months when Andie cannot uncover an alternative, her own name is drawn from the virgin lottery.<br /><br />Although Andie befriends the Champion sent by Godmother Elena (from the first book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13982.The_Fairy_Godmother__Five_Hundred_Kingdoms___1_" title="The Fairy Godmother (Five Hundred Kingdoms, #1) by Mercedes Lackey" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fairy Godmother</a>) to rescue her, Andie - with the help of a clever fable fox - quickly discovers the dragon is not the danger it seems. <br /><br />Adamant is a Warrior dragon who has been compelled by a geas to raid; with the help of his learned Bookwyrm brother Periapt, he is trying to find a way free from the spell. Although they cannot break it, they can twist it, so they have gathered all the sacrificial (and very much alive) maidens together in a rough sort of army, and when Andie arrives they have enough momentum to manipulate The Tradition to help them seek justice. <br /><br />There are two unconventional love stories that thankfully have Happily Ever After endings, but to say anything more would ruin the great twist ending. The last line was a little weak and jokey but otherwise this is a wonderful modern fairy tale!<br /><br />Minor quibble: There are two separate minor characters with the same name, a Lady Thalia and a maiden Thalia. This is incredibly confusing, and for some reason seems to happen a lot in Lackey books. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14629407102686454426" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  <span id="freeText6706132684597688854" style="display:none">So much fun. I would really have loved the series when I was an innocent young teen lo these several decades ago. Then the little bits of awkward writing mechanics and occasional errors &amp; inconsistencies wouldn't have bothered me at all. I would simply have been enchanted by fascinating world-building and all the different characters, many of whom are females who are strong and smart and wicked and lazy and etc. in all sorts of different ways.<br /><br />I'm becoming such a fan of Lackey I plan not only to read all books in this set but maybe find another book or series by her.<br /><br />Btw, the first book in the 500 Kingdoms does have some sexy bits that I would not have been ready for until I was about 14. This one is not only at least as easy to read but is also 'clean' enough for even a 12 yo. Oh, hey, but don't get me wrong, by easy I don't mean trite. There's plenty here to spark a reader's imagination and even to provoke discussion in a book club.<br /><br />And there's quotable bits. "'[We're] clever and cunning, not intelligent," the fox corrected absently. "Not the same thing at all.'"</span>

<div id="review_373934909" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/373934909" />
    <a title="TheCosyDragon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7846533-thecosydragon"><img alt="TheCosyDragon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421894417p2/7846533.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/373934909?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TheCosyDragon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TheCosyDragon" href="/user/show/7846533-thecosydragon">TheCosyDragon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer373934909" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12086018897066038658">This review has been crossposted from my blog at <a href='http://www.thecosydragon.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Cosy Dragon </a>. Please head there for more in-depth reviews by me, which appear on a timely schedule.<br/><br/>Princess Andie is intelligent, waif-like beautiful and has just turned 19. Her mother however isn't ready to see her as an adult, and would rather she was confused and silly with conventional beauty. When Andie finally gets a real 'job', she uncovers things that were probably better off hidden. Andie becomes a liability very quickly - as a virgin</span>
  <span id="freeText12086018897066038658" style="display:none">This review has been crossposted from my blog at <a href="http://www.thecosydragon.com" rel="nofollow noopener">The Cosy Dragon </a>. Please head there for more in-depth reviews by me, which appear on a timely schedule.<br /><br />Princess Andie is intelligent, waif-like beautiful and has just turned 19. Her mother however isn't ready to see her as an adult, and would rather she was confused and silly with conventional beauty. When Andie finally gets a real 'job', she uncovers things that were probably better off hidden. Andie becomes a liability very quickly - as a virgin she's very likely to be snaffled up by an evil creature...<br /><br />Andie is smart, and bookish - just what I like in a female protagonist. She isn't very good with common things, but her common sense is certainly in place. Yay for a non-traditional heir. Lackey has a good thing going, and she really works with it.<br /><br />The different perspectives of this book, particularly the Queen vs Andie in the first parts of the book really set the plot going. Those that have read The Fairy Godmother in this series will recognise the Traditional path that is taking place, but Andie can't see it. You just keep waiting for the penny to drop!<br /><br />So many good things to say about this book, but many of them would give away too much of the plot. It's not a particularly hard read, but it will sucker you in and steal all of your time (oops to doing all that study I had lined up)<br /><br />Andie's knowledge of the Tradition, and also that of the other people in her Kingdom (such as Sophont Balen) seems strange, after the emphasis in The Fairy Godmother about most people having no idea. Yet everyone seems to be exploiting it easily! It's nice to see how a situation can be resolved without a Fairy Godmother though - the regular people have a chance.<br /><br />The cover of this book doesn't match how I saw Andie at all. I though she was very thin with no breasts, and the girl on the cover certainly does have those! Also I expected that the dragon would be less fierce looking than that. Hard to discuss more without giving the plot away.<br /><br />Worth a read. I'd say this book is suitable for teens as well as adults because it contains none of the explicit sex scenes of the first book. This series is a very good one, and worth buying to reread often. Lackey really breaths life into old fairytales.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12086018897066038658" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_157817033" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/157817033" />
    <a title="Ana Mardoll" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3078990-ana-mardoll"><img alt="Ana Mardoll" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1519954099p2/3078990.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/157817033?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ana Mardoll" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ana Mardoll" href="/user/show/3078990-ana-mardoll">Ana Mardoll</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3078990-ana-mardoll?shelf=ana-reviewed">ana-reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer157817033" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10861707745631405715">One Good Knight / 978-0-373-80260-9<br/><br/>I rather enjoy the Five Hundred Kingdoms books - starting with "The Fairy Godmother" and continuing to the recent fifth book "The Sleeping Beauty". The tales are something of a mixed-up fairy tale due to the unique backstory: a powerful and impersonal force called The Tradition constantly tries to impose "fairy tale" logic on people whose lives loosely fit the structure of commonly told fairy tales, and Godmothers and Champions devote their lives trying to faci</span>
  <span id="freeText10861707745631405715" style="display:none">One Good Knight / 978-0-373-80260-9<br /><br />I rather enjoy the Five Hundred Kingdoms books - starting with "The Fairy Godmother" and continuing to the recent fifth book "The Sleeping Beauty". The tales are something of a mixed-up fairy tale due to the unique backstory: a powerful and impersonal force called The Tradition constantly tries to impose "fairy tale" logic on people whose lives loosely fit the structure of commonly told fairy tales, and Godmothers and Champions devote their lives trying to facilitate the happy endings and thwart the bad ones that The Tradition tries to impose.<br /><br />This is the second book in the loosely connected series, and I have to admit that I enjoyed it a bit more than its predecessor, "The Fairy Godmother" - probably for the same reasons that others *didn't*. The major differences here is that "One Good Knight" is slightly shorter (an approximate 400 pages to TFG's 500), and their is significantly less emphasis on romance and much more emphasis on the given fractured fairy tale (a mash-up of the Greek Andromeda myth and the English 'George and the Dragon' tale). Judge your own tastes accordingly - if what you most enjoyed about TFG was the romance and world-building, you may want to give this a pass; if you prefer the fractured fairy tale concept, then I can almost guarantee you will enjoy this novel.<br /><br />Like all the Lackey novels I've read so far, the plot is quite gripping, the characterizations are superb, and the dialogue has a tendency to make me laugh out loud regularly. Lackey specializes in well-rounded and strong female characters, and "One Good Knight" does not disappoint - it's nice to have a "plain" and bookish princess for once (even if the cover artist didn't get the memo, an ongoing gripe I have with this series, see also "The Sleeping Beauty"). If I had one criticism about this book, it would be that some of the ending feels a little rushed and confusing; the pacing at the middle should have been tightened, I think, to allow the ending to flow more naturally. I'm not usually a fan of end-game exposition dumps, but I think a tiny one could have been employed here.<br /><br />I enjoyed this novel immensely, though, and definitely recommend it for fans of the series.<br /><br />~ Ana Mardoll</span>
  <a data-text-id="10861707745631405715" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_255330367" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/255330367" />
    <a title="Lynnae" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6857573-lynnae"><img alt="Lynnae" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1321576260p2/6857573.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/255330367?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lynnae" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lynnae" href="/user/show/6857573-lynnae">Lynnae</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fairy-tale lovers, Lackey fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6857573-lynnae?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer255330367" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3180844921998903580">As fairy tale retellings go, this was fantastic! Lackey breaks many of the fairy tale tropes by shamelessly mixing and merging many well-known stories in the grab-bag of her Five Hundred Kingdoms. She's done an excellent job of building a world that allows her exactly that freedom, paying homage to the original tales and using them to inform and guide her characters' actions as they re-craft the story for themselves. <br/><br/>I enjoy self-aware stories, where the characters exhibit the intelligence to kn</span>
  <span id="freeText3180844921998903580" style="display:none">As fairy tale retellings go, this was fantastic! Lackey breaks many of the fairy tale tropes by shamelessly mixing and merging many well-known stories in the grab-bag of her Five Hundred Kingdoms. She's done an excellent job of building a world that allows her exactly that freedom, paying homage to the original tales and using them to inform and guide her characters' actions as they re-craft the story for themselves. <br /><br />I enjoy self-aware stories, where the characters exhibit the intelligence to know that they are affecting their own story. Lackey is a self-aware author, as well. She knows that she is bending the rules, and she does it artfully. <br /><br />With One Good Knight, I was kept on my toes as I tried to figure out just which fairy tale she was telling. At first glance, it looks like Sir George and the Dragon, but it soon breaks very obviously from that storyline and follows a new path that looks like Robin Hood, Cinderella, and Snow White, all rolled into one. <br /><br />Andromeda is an interesting character. She is a princess, but unlike many Beauty and the Beast stories, she's not a beauty who simply doesn't see herself clearly. Her flaws and handicaps are never magically done away, so that suddenly she is no longer a misfit princess. Instead, she remains slightly misfit, but she learns how to live with it. Occasionally, her self-deprecation was a little tiresome, and I truly enjoyed the scenes with Gina, who serves as a foil to Andromeda. So much so that I half-wanted Gina to get her own story. <br /><br />I'll admit that the book got frustrating occasionally. Lackey's break with the traditional line of fairy-tale-telling means that you're not entirely sure where the story is going. Characters don't do what you think they're going to do, and the change from the original story sometimes makes it feel like you're missing something. <br /><br />But at the same time, that is the appeal of Lackey's approach---She's not telling the same story that's been told a hundred times already. She takes the story you think you know, and manages to surprise you with it. <br /><br />I'd recommend it to readers looking for a fresh version of an old fairy tale.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3180844921998903580" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50581-lydia-presley?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50581-lydia-presley?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50581-lydia-presley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer130809237" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer5134365042124039621">It's sometimes difficult to write a review of a book in a series, because you don't want to reveal anything from the books before. So while I could gush on and on about how awesome it was to see familiar characters in this book in detail, I'll.. spare you the detail and just say that One Good Knight solidified my love for Mercedes Lackey.<br/><br/>Seriously, y'all, I have so much fun reading these books.<br/><br/>I think, in a way, this book was almost better than the first... because it didn't require as much sett</span>
  <span id="freeText5134365042124039621" style="display:none">It's sometimes difficult to write a review of a book in a series, because you don't want to reveal anything from the books before. So while I could gush on and on about how awesome it was to see familiar characters in this book in detail, I'll.. spare you the detail and just say that One Good Knight solidified my love for Mercedes Lackey.<br /><br />Seriously, y'all, I have so much fun reading these books.<br /><br />I think, in a way, this book was almost better than the first... because it didn't require as much setting up as the first did. That said, it still did require some, but it was the perfect set-up for the story to shift in a way that had me sitting up and saying.. "What?!".<br /><br />... oh no, I'm not going to tell you what had me saying that, you just need to trust me when I say these are fun, fantasy books well worth reading.<br /><br />And can I just say... I love what Mercedes Lackey does with the unicorns. The image of unicorns going all doe-eyed and docile, panting over virgin girls has me dying of laughter every time I see them make an appearance. And what impressed me most about this book? There was romance with absolutely ZERO sexual scenes described. None! And still, I swooned and sighed with happiness. <br /><br />And most importantly - the girls in these books.. HAVE BRAINS! And they use them! They are intelligent, witty, and brave! So marvelous!<br /><br />Fantastic series and I'm going to start the next book as soon as I finish this review - I recommend you start with The Fairy Godmother and work your way through them as well, if you haven't already!</span>

<div id="review_157188467" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/157188467" />
    <a title="Jessie  (Ageless Pages Reviews)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews"><img alt="Jessie  (Ageless Pages Reviews)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603380977p2/4863162.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/157188467?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessie  (Ageless Pages Reviews)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessie  (Ageless Pages Reviews)" href="/user/show/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews">Jessie  (Ageless Pages Reviews)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781426861987" href="/book/show/8594785-one-good-knight">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews?shelf=tales-of-fae-and-faery-tales">tales-of-fae-and-faery-tales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews?shelf=2011-reads">2011-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews?shelf=mythic-fiction">mythic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews?shelf=here-be-monsters">here-be-monsters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews?shelf=nook-books">nook-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews?shelf=series-ongoing">series-ongoing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews?shelf=reviews-2011">reviews-2011</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer157188467" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8396691272695163463">This was a drastic improvement over the first in the series of the Five Hundred Kingdoms. Almost none of the problems I had from the first novel were in this sequel, and it was vastly more entertaining to read than <i>The Fairy Godmother</i>. Instead of focusing on the "Cinderella" fairytale, the second book is about the Greek legend of the Andromeda sacrifices in a small, poor Kingdom with no Godmother.<br/>First on the list of vast improvements is Andromeda herself. Andie is the main character and is actu</span>
  <span id="freeText8396691272695163463" style="display:none">This was a drastic improvement over the first in the series of the Five Hundred Kingdoms. Almost none of the problems I had from the first novel were in this sequel, and it was vastly more entertaining to read than <i>The Fairy Godmother</i>. Instead of focusing on the "Cinderella" fairytale, the second book is about the Greek legend of the Andromeda sacrifices in a small, poor Kingdom with no Godmother.<br />First on the list of vast improvements is Andromeda herself. Andie is the main character and is actually that, a character instead of a cliche. She's smart, bookish, resourceful, and clever. She's a very engaging character, as were the villains of the story (which surprised me).<br />Second on the list, the conflict and resolution did not seem nearly as rushed as the end of the first book. The entire novel felt more well-planned, thought out and written. It's also much funnier and filled with more fleshed out characters instead of one-dimensional second-rate "personalities".<br />One minor problem I had was that sometimes the actions of a character would make absolutely no sense, as in did nothing to help that character out and were blatant attempts to make the ending work to its <s>predictable</s> Traditional path. That being said, the ending did surprise me in a way that I totally loved and grinned while reading.<br />A <i>much</i> better book than the first and I look forward to the next.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8396691272695163463" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65650827-chi?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65650827-chi?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65650827-chi?shelf=retelling">retelling</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65650827-chi?shelf=fantasy-romance">fantasy-romance</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2040413955" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11899514736581086725"><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Bookwyrm. /snigger<br/>That was inspired. XD <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br/><br/>This started out so Boring... so Boring, that I had to capitalise it. There was just so much world-building (in this Greece-like corner of the Five Hundred Kingdoms), and exploration of Andromeda's (or more affectionately known as Andie) life that that first half of the book at least, DRAGGED on. I appreciated that Mercedes Lackey had used Andromeda (and her mother, Cassiopeia) as the basis of the story, and felt that it was a</span>
  <span id="freeText11899514736581086725" style="display:none"><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Bookwyrm. /snigger<br />That was inspired. XD <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />This started out so Boring... so Boring, that I had to capitalise it. There was just so much world-building (in this Greece-like corner of the Five Hundred Kingdoms), and exploration of Andromeda's (or more affectionately known as Andie) life that that first half of the book at least, DRAGGED on. I appreciated that Mercedes Lackey had used Andromeda (and her mother, Cassiopeia) as the basis of the story, and felt that it was an especially nice touch to set it in what was a fair approximation of Greece, far away from the bog standard English medieval setting. But it was still tiresome.<br /><br />And then, the story picked up, right about when Andie was sacrificed to the dragon. That's when things got really interesting. And even fun, as some pivotal secondary characters got introduced.<br /><br />While it was a shame that the romance aspect of the book didn't kick in until a good three-quarters of the way through, I loved that it was of a melding of minds, rather than of looks. The secondary romance didn't hurt either because the ending was just perfect, and oh so sweet. So far that, I was happy to forgive the first portion of the book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11899514736581086725" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2431873-emily?shelf=sci-fi-fantasy">sci-fi-fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer64184162" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13983434783245593748">This book hovers between two and three stars, simply because I found the plot and characters to be rather boring. The characters are all two-dimensional, predictable, and stereotypical, and the hastily contrived romantic ending added nothing to the novel.<br/><br/>The real draw of this book - why I liked it despite myself - was "The Tradition," which is a magical force that acts upon the residents of the Five Hundred Kingdoms. Essentially, the Tradition requires that people act as it wants them to: freed </span>
  <span id="freeText13983434783245593748" style="display:none">This book hovers between two and three stars, simply because I found the plot and characters to be rather boring. The characters are all two-dimensional, predictable, and stereotypical, and the hastily contrived romantic ending added nothing to the novel.<br /><br />The real draw of this book - why I liked it despite myself - was "The Tradition," which is a magical force that acts upon the residents of the Five Hundred Kingdoms. Essentially, the Tradition requires that people act as it wants them to: freed maidens always fall in love with their rescuers, the first two sons always fail in the quest, etc. Characters can work with or against the Tradition, mixing the tropes of every fantasy novel together. For example, in order to avoid the compulsion she feels to fall in love with her rescuer, the princess makes a blood sibling oath with him; immediately the compulsion is lifted, and they travel onward. For someone who has read an embarrassing amount of fantasy in the past, this was an amusing and fresh take on the cliches of every fantasy. I just wish the plot and characters could have drawn more of my interest.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13983434783245593748" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/135413365?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Janus the Erudite Artist" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Janus the Erudite Artist" href="/user/show/4552491-janus-the-erudite-artist">Janus the Erudite Artist</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4552491-janus-the-erudite-artist?shelf=owned-paperback">owned-paperback</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer135413365" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9062522212014362525">I've seen a number of reviewers not pleased with One Good Knight. When I read it myself, I had mixed feelings about it. My mind has been switching from liking to not then liking it again, and then not...again. By the ending I was really confused. <br/><br/>I enjoyed reading the book, don't get me wrong. I was really pleased to see this take lesser pages than Lackey's other books that tended to be so descriptive. I also found the characters very likeable and the twist with regards to the champion was reall</span>
  <span id="freeText9062522212014362525" style="display:none">I've seen a number of reviewers not pleased with One Good Knight. When I read it myself, I had mixed feelings about it. My mind has been switching from liking to not then liking it again, and then not...again. By the ending I was really confused. <br /><br />I enjoyed reading the book, don't get me wrong. I was really pleased to see this take lesser pages than Lackey's other books that tended to be so descriptive. I also found the characters very likeable and the twist with regards to the champion was really sneaky! And I absolutely did not expect it. <br /><br />What bothered me was that I didn't get to know the villains that much. There was a constant mystery about their agenda with each scene that they appear at but there wasn't much of a revelation in the end. <br /><br />Also, as much as I liked the "happily ever after" thing with Lackey's stories. I think this was a bit too much of a cliche. I get that this is a fairy tale after all and I'm happy for the characters but there wasn't much to it to commend about. <br /><br />Overall I think it was okay, plus points on being more fast paced than the other books... and it wasn't as bad as I thought it would be.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9062522212014362525" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer84019519" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8239796825121099136">I've been on a Mercedes Lackey kick for the past year or so, and it's always a little disappointing. The problem when you crank out 50+ books is that you tend to sacrifice quality for quantity.<br/><br/>Despite this, I love her stories (if not the actual writing). Especially this series. She actually takes a really interesting premise - people forced to adhere to archetypes (from myths, fairy tales, and fables), and makes an engaging story. Could it be more awesome? Yes. Is it pretty good anyway? Also yes</span>
  <span id="freeText8239796825121099136" style="display:none">I've been on a Mercedes Lackey kick for the past year or so, and it's always a little disappointing. The problem when you crank out 50+ books is that you tend to sacrifice quality for quantity.<br /><br />Despite this, I love her stories (if not the actual writing). Especially this series. She actually takes a really interesting premise - people forced to adhere to archetypes (from myths, fairy tales, and fables), and makes an engaging story. Could it be more awesome? Yes. Is it pretty good anyway? Also yes. This is like fluffy cotton candy for my brain.<br /><br />Highly recommended for anyone who likes myths, fairy tales, and/or fables, and kickass characters (mostly of the female variety).</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZdcGMUryOg07vu0N1sZjMjb9oALsp2VW+FsmKkGDUuvUIX91exE4mGADQp6EMqK3elwYeiyTlD4+MNS74yyojA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('q1bZ2VtRRIMkfdCFciJ6HjkY4x8YTSkgBq4SiwYZUYAaoKCdarJGFn/AfxYg1rubdblbZ9h52EjAxeAapLar5w==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/8685.Mercedes_Lackey">About Mercedes Lackey</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/8685.Mercedes_Lackey"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1215643156p3/8685.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/8685.Mercedes_Lackey">Mercedes Lackey

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3469553856810182515">Mercedes entered this world on June 24, 1950, in Chicago, had a normal childhood and graduated from Purdue University in 1972. During the late 70's she worked as an artist's model and then went into the computer programming field, ending up with American Airlines in Tulsa, Oklahoma. In addition to her fantasy writing, she has written lyrics for and recorded nearly fifty songs for Firebird Arts & M</span>
  <span id="freeText3469553856810182515" style="display:none">Mercedes entered this world on June 24, 1950, in Chicago, had a normal childhood and graduated from Purdue University in 1972. During the late 70's she worked as an artist's model and then went into the computer programming field, ending up with American Airlines in Tulsa, Oklahoma. In addition to her fantasy writing, she has written lyrics for and recorded nearly fifty songs for Firebird Arts &amp; Music, a small recording company specializing in science fiction folk music.<br /><br />"I'm a storyteller; that's what I see as 'my job'. My stories come out of my characters; how those characters would react to the given situation. Maybe that's why I get letters from readers as young as thirteen and as old as sixty-odd. One of the reasons I write song lyrics is because I see songs as a kind of 'story pill' -- they reduce a story to the barest essentials or encapsulate a particular crucial moment in time. I frequently will write a lyric when I am attempting to get to the heart of a crucial scene; I find that when I have done so, the scene has become absolutely clear in my mind, and I can write exactly what I wanted to say. Another reason is because of the kind of novels I am writing: that is, fantasy, set in an other-world semi-medieval atmosphere. Music is very important to medieval peoples; bards are the chief newsbringers. When I write the 'folk music' of these peoples, I am enriching my whole world, whether I actually use the song in the text or not.<br /><br />"I began writing out of boredom; I continue out of addiction. I can't 'not' write, and as a result I have no social life! I began writing fantasy because I love it, but I try to construct my fantasy worlds with all the care of a 'high-tech' science fiction writer. I apply the principle of TANSTAAFL ['There ain't no such thing as free lunch', credited to Robert Heinlein) to magic, for instance; in my worlds, magic is paid for, and the cost to the magician is frequently a high one. I try to keep my world as solid and real as possible; people deal with stubborn pumps, bugs in the porridge, and love-lives that refuse to become untangled, right along with invading armies and evil magicians. And I try to make all of my characters, even the 'evil magicians,' something more than flat stereotypes. Even evil magicians get up in the night and look for cookies, sometimes.<br /><br />"I suppose that in everything I write I try to expound the creed I gave my character Diana Tregarde in <i>Burning Water</i>:<br /><br />"There's no such thing as 'one, true way'; the only answers worth having are the ones you find for yourself; leave the world better than you found it. Love, freedom, and the chance to do some good -- they're the things worth living and dying for, and if you aren't willing to die for the things worth living for, you might as well turn in your membership in the human race." <br /><br />Also writes as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2504886.Misty_Lackey" rel="nofollow noopener">Misty Lackey</a><br /><br /><a href="http://us.macmillan.com/author/mercedeslackey" rel="nofollow noopener">Author's website</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3469553856810182515" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

            <span class="readable">&ldquo;This had to be the most curious situation in all of her life. Not that she had a great deal to compare it to, of course, living, as she had, quite a sheltered existence. But if anyone had ever had a friend quite like Periapt, she had yet to read about it.<br />The most peculiar thing was the feeling, the conviction, that here was someone she had been looking for as a friend and companion her entire life.<br />When they were talking and she wasn't actually looking at him- in the dark, say, when they would go up to the top of the tower to rest their eyes and look at the stars- she never, ever even <i>thought</i> about the fact that he was a dragon. In fact, if she was reading a book with him and he would say something aloud, she would get a kind of shock to her system when she looked up and saw, not a person, but a huge, dusky-emerald dragon head.<br />The shock was getting worse, too, not better, every time she looked up and didn't see the studious young man she expected to see.&rdquo;</span>
